1 Scope 1
This Technical Specification has been produced by the O-RAN Alliance. 2
The contents of the present document are subject to continuing work within O-RAN and may change following formal 3
O-RAN approval. Should the O-RAN Alliance modify the contents of the present document, it will be re-released by O-4
RAN with an identifying change of release date and an increase in version number as follows:  5
Release x.y.z 6
where: 7
x the first digit is incremented for all changes of substance, i.e. technical enhancements, corrections, updates, 8
etc. (the initial approved document will have x=01). 9
y the second digit is incremented when editorial only changes have been incorporated in the document.  10
z the third digit included only in working versions of the document indicating incremental changes during the 11
editing process. 12
The present document specifies the E2 Service Model (E2SM) for the Near RT RIC RAN Control interaction. 13

  15

4 General 1
4.1 Procedure Specification Principles 2
The principle for specifying the procedure logic is to specify the functional behaviour of the terminating node exactly 3
and completely. Any rule that specifies the behaviour of the originating node shall be possible to be verified with 4
information that is visible within the system. 5
The following specification principles have been applied for the procedure text in clause 8:  6
- The procedure text discriminates between: 7
1) Functionality which "shall" be executed. 8
 The procedure text indicates that the receiving node "shall" perform a certain function Y under a certain 9
condition. If the receiving node supports procedure X but cannot perform functionality Y requested in the 10
REQUEST message of a Class 1 EP, the receiving node shall respond with the message used to report 11
unsuccessful outcome for this procedure, containing an appropriate cause value.  12
2) Functionality which "shall, if supported" be executed. 13
 The procedure text indicates that the receiving node "shall, if supported," perform a certain function Y under 14
a certain condition. If the receiving node supports procedure X, but does not support functionality Y, the 15
receiving node shall proceed with the execution of the EP, possibly informing the requesting node about the 16
not supported functionality. 17
- Any required inclusion of an optional IE in a response message is explicitly indicated in the procedure text. If the 18
procedure text does not explicitly indicate that an optional IE shall be included in a response message, the 19
optional IE shall not be included. For requirements on including Criticality Diagnostics IE, see clause 10. 20
4.2 Forwards and Backwards Compatibility 21
The forwards and backwards compatibility of the protocol is assured by a mechanism where all current and future 22
messages, and IEs or groups of related IEs, include ID and criticality fields that are coded in a standard format that will 23
not be changed in the future. These parts can always be decoded regardless of  the standard version. 24
4.3 Specification Notations 25
For the purposes of the present document, the following notations apply: 26
Service when referring to a Service in the specification the SERVICE NAME is written with upper case 27
characters and in bold followed by the word "service", e.g. REPORT service. 28
Procedure When referring to an elementary procedure in the specification the Procedure Name is written with 29
the first letters in each word in upper case characters followed by the word "procedure", e.g. 30
Handover Preparation procedure. 31
Message When referring to a message in the specification the MESSAGE NAME is written with all letters 32
in upper case characters followed by the word "message", e.g. HANDOVER REQUEST message.  33
IE When referring to an information element (IE) in the specification the Information Element Name 34
is written with the first letters in each word in upper case characters and all letters in Italic font 35
followed by the abbreviation "IE", e.g. E-RAB ID IE. 36
Value of an IE When referring to the value of an information element (IE) in the specification the "Value" is 37
written as it is specified in the specification enclosed by quotation marks, e.g. "Value".  38

6 RAN Function Service Model Description 1
6.1 RAN Function Overview 2
For the purposes of this E2 Service Model, E2SM-RC, the E2 Node terminating the E2 Interface is assumed to host one 3
or more instances of the RAN Function “RAN Control” which performs the following functionalities:  4
- E2 REPORT services used to expose RAN control and UE context related information  5
- E2 INSERT services used to suspend RAN control related call processes 6
- E2 CONTROL services used to resume or initiate RAN control related call processes, modify RAN 7
configuration and/or E2 service-related UE context information 8
- E2 POLICY services used to modify the behaviour of RAN control related processes  9
This E2SM specification provides a set of RAN Function exposure services described in clause 6.2 and has been 10
prepared with the assumption that the same E2SM may be used to describe either a single RAN Function in the E2 11
Node handling all RAN control related call processes or more than one RAN Function in the E2 Node with each 12
instance handling a subset of the RAN control related call processes on the E2 Node.  13
6.2 RAN Function exposure services 14
6.2.1 REPORT service 15
The “RAN Control” RAN Function provides selective support of the following REPORT  services: 16
- Copy of Complete message (from Network Interface or RRC), used for monitoring POLICY services, data 17
gathering (to populate the Near-RT RIC UE-NIB and/or ML services data pipeline), etc. 18
- Call process outcome with associated information on UE context and/or RAN status information, used for 19
monitoring [CONTROL and] POLICY services, data gathering (to populate the Near- RT RIC UE-NIB and/or 20
ML services data pipeline), etc.  21
- E2 Node Information and Cell related Information, used for monitoring of E2 Node and Cell configuration 22
changes, triggering POLICY deletion, changing notifications (to reset Near-RT RIC optimization services), etc.   23
- UE Information, used for monitoring of UE information changes, triggering E2 Control, location tracking, etc.  24
- On Demand Report, used for reporting Cell related, E2 Node related and UE related information to Near -RT RIC 25
when requested by Near-RT RIC. 26
NOTE: Only the UE with user consent can be configured to report location information.  27
6.2.2 INSERT service 28
The “RAN Control” RAN Function provides selective support of the following INSERT services: 29
Fundamental level: 30
- Radio Bearer Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control DRB QoS modification, QoS flow to DRB 31
(re)mapping, Logical channel (re)configuration, Radio bearer admission control, Split bearer and PDCP duplication 32
control, etc. 33
- Radio Resource Allocation Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control Discontinuous Reception 34
(DRX), Scheduling request (SR), Semi-Persistent Scheduling (SPS), Configured Grant, Channel Quality 35
Indicator (CQI) table, Slice level PRB quota, etc. 36
- Connected Mode Mobility Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control operations of Handover (HO), 37
Conditional handover (CHO), Dual Active Protocol Stack (DAPS) HO, etc. 38
- Radio Access Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control parameters related to RACH back- off, 39
RRC connection reject, RRC connection release, Access barring, UE admission, etc.  40

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.02
Copyright © 2022 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ
 15
- Dual Connectivity (DC) Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control operations of Dual Connectivity 1
(DC) including Change of bearer termination point (MN or SN) and/or bearer types, etc.  2
- Carrier Aggregation (CA) Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control operations of Carrier 3
Aggregation (CA) involving secondary cell re-selection. 4
- Idle Mode Mobility Control request, used for requesting the RIC to control intra -frequency, inter-frequency, 5

- Multiple Actions Control request, used for requesting the RIC to command multiple actions of the selected 9

6.2.3 CONTROL service 12
The “RAN Control” RAN Function provides selective support of the following CONTROL  services: 13
Fundamental level: 14
- Radio Bearer Control, used for DRB QoS modification, QoS flow to DRB (re)mapping, Logical channel 15
(re)configuration, Radio bearer admission control, Split bearer and PDCP duplication control, etc.  16
- Radio Resource Allocation Control, used to control Discontinuous Reception (DRX), Scheduling request (SR), 17
Semi-Persistent Scheduling (SPS), Configured Grant, Channel Quality Indicator (CQI) table,  Slice level PRB 18
quota, etc. 19
- Connected Mode Mobility Control, used to control operations of Handover (HO), Conditional handover (CHO), 20
Dual Active Protocol Stack (DAPS) HO, etc. 21
- Radio Access Control, used for modification of RACH back-off, RRC connection reject, RRC connection 22
release, Access barring, UE admission, etc. 23
- Dual Connectivity (DC) Control, used to control operations of Dual Connectivity (DC) including Change of 24
bearer termination point (MN or SN) and/or bearer types, etc. 25
- Carrier Aggregation (CA) Control, used to control operations of Carrier Aggregation (CA ). 26
- Idle Mode Mobility Control, used for modification of intra-frequency, inter-frequency, inter-RAT cell 27
reselection priority, idle timers, etc.  28
- UE to RAN UE group assignment, used to support POLICY services. 29
- Measurement Report (MR) Configuration Control, used to control configuration of RRC measurement objects, 30
reporting objects, etc. 31
 32
Integrated level: 33
- Multiple Actions Control, used to command multiple actions of the selected fundamental level CONTROL 34
services in one message. 35
 36
6.2.4 POLICY service 37
The “RAN Control” RAN Function provides selective support of the following POLICY services: 38
- Radio Bearer Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to DRB QoS control, QoS flow to 39
DRB mapping, Logical channel configuration, Radio bearer admission control, Split bearer and PDCP 40
duplication control, etc. 41
- Radio Resource Allocation Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes  related to DRX, SR, SPS, 42
Configured Grant, CQI table, Slice level PRB quota, etc. 43

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.02
Copyright © 2022 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ
 16
- Connected Mode Mobility Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to HO, CHO, DAPS 1
HO, etc. for both serving and target RAN nodes. 2
- Radio Access Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to RACH back- off, RRC connection 3
reject, RRC connection release, Access barring, UE admission, etc. 4
- Dual Connectivity (DC) Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to DC rel ated operations 5
for both master and secondary RAN nodes, Change of bearer termination point (MN or SN) and/or bearer types, 6
etc. 7
- Carrier Aggregation (CA) Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to CA related operations 8
for both primary and secondary cells. 9
- Idle Mode Mobility Policy, used to modify the behaviour of call processes related to intra -frequency, inter-10
frequency, inter-RAT cell reselection priority, inactivity timers, etc. 11
- Measurement Report (MR) Configuration Policy, used to configure policy for RRC measurement objects, 12
reporting objects, etc. 13
6.3 REPORT service description 14
The E2SM-RC REPORT service requirements defined in Section 6.2.1 are offered using a set of REPORT Styles.  All 15
REPORT styles are implemented using a set of IEs for Action Definition, RIC Indication Header and RIC Indication 16
Message and have specific Event Trigger approach. For each Report style, a single RAN Parameter table is used to 17
specify the required information to be reported. 18
The following REPORT styles are supported:  19
- Message copy: This REPORT style is initiated by “Message Event” Event Trigger and is used to report complete 20
NI or RRC message along with UE associated information when the event trigger conditions are satisfied.  21
- Call Process Outcome: This REPORT style is initiated by the corresponding "Call Process Breakpoint" Event 22
Trigger and is used to report on the outcome of a call process providing information on current, and in certain 23
cases previous, UE or E2 Node information depending upon the nature of the target call process.   24
- E2 Node Information: This REPORT style is initiated by “E2 Node Information Change” Event Trigger and is 25
used to report cell related and E2 Node related information upon event trigger conditions are satisf ied. 26
- UE information: This REPORT style is initiated by “UE Information Change” Event Trigger and is used to 27
report UE related information and UE state variables upon the event trigger conditions are satisfied.  28
- On demand report: This REPORT style is initiated by “On Demand” Event Trigger and is used to report cell -29
related and UE-related information on an adhoc basis upon request from Near-RT RIC. 30
6.4 INSERT service description 31
The E2SM-RC INSERT service requirements defined in Section 6.2.2 are offered using a set of INSERT Styles. Each 32
style corresponds to a set of “INSERT Indications”, where each “INSERT Indication” deals with a specific functionality  33
and has a set of associated RAN parameters, provided in a mapping table. All INSERT Service styles are implemented 34
using a set of IEs that constitute “Action Definition”, “RIC Indication Header” and “RIC Indication Message” to deliver 35
RAN Control-related INSERT services. Each INSERT service style is associated with a specific “Event Trigger” 36
approach.  An “INSERT Indication” is used to request the RIC to control a functionality associated with the respective 37
INSERT service style, and to set or modify the values of one or more associated RAN parameters.  38
As an example, upon the arrival of an RRC Measurement Report in the E2 node due to the occurrence of an A3 event 39
pertaining to a UE (which constitutes the event trigger), the E2 node can send a  message to the RIC using the 40
“Connected Mode Mobility” INSERT service style and the “Handover Control Re quest” INSERT Indication along with 41
the “target cell ID” parameter. This RIC should then accept/deny the “Handover Control Request”, and if it accepts, it 42
should set the value of the “target cell ID” parameter and send a CONTROL action back to the RIC. Up until then, the 43
E2 node suspends the ongoing call processing for the UE.  44

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.02
Copyright © 2022 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ
 17
6.5 CONTROL service description 1
The E2SM-RC CONTROL service requirements defined in Section 6.2.3 are offered using a set of CONTROL Styles. 2
Each style corresponds to a set of “CONTROL Action”, where each “CONTROL Action” deals with a specific 3
functionality and has a set of associated RAN parameters, provided in a mapping table. All CONTROL Service styles 4
are implemented using a set of IEs constituting a “RIC Control Request Header” a nd a “RIC Control Request Message” 5
to deliver RAN Control-related CONTROL services. A “CONTROL Action” containing one or more RAN parameters 6
and their associated values can either be sent from the RIC, either asynchronously to the E2 node or as a response to a 7
previous “INSERT Indication” from the E2 node.  8
Referring to the previous example in Section 6.4, the RIC sends a “CONTROL action” that accepts/denies the incoming 9
“INSERT Indication” requesting for “Handover Control”, along with the value of the “Tar get Primary Cell”. As another 10
example, the RIC can also asynchronously send a “CONTROL action” asking the E2 node to configure the UE in 11
Carrier Aggregation mode and setup one or more secondary cells to the UE, whose values are assigned by the RIC via 12
the “CONTROL action”. 13
6.6 POLICY service description 14
6.6.1 Overview 15
The E2SM-RC POLICY service requirements defined in Section 6.2.4 are offered using a set of POLICY Styles.  Each 16
style is implemented using multiple "Policy Approach" strategies, each with a s pecific methodology defined to use the 17
E2AP IE "Action Definition" to deliver RAN Control related POLICY services.  18
The following Policy Approaches are defined: 19
- Control: POLICY for a given Style and Action ID is defined as a single case of a specific Policy condition with 20
the corresponding Policy Action defined using the same data structure as CONTROL which would be used to 21
replace default RAN behaviour. 22
- Offset: POLICY for a given Style and Action ID is defined as a set of different cases ap plicable for a range of 23
different Policy conditions with the corresponding Policy Action defined using the dedicated data structure 24
defined for POLICY which would be used to modify default RAN behaviour.  25
6.6.2 Policy approach "Control" 26
The “control” Policy Approach is similar to the CONTROL service, with static conditions and actions in the RIC 27
Subscription used to select an appropriate CONTROL Action. When a set of Policy conditions are satisfied, then E2 28
Node is instructed to execute a Policy Action with a set of supplementary or default set of RAN parameters.  29
A single Policy Action shall be a result of execution of multiple policy conditions.  30
- Each Policy Condition is defined using a combination of RAN Parameters and conditional tests associated with 31
UE and Call process related information. 32
- Each Policy Action is defined with a single Policy Action ID (command) which instructs E2 Node to perform a 33
certain action when the conditions are satisfied. The Policy Action ID shall be supplemented with a set of RAN 34
Parameters which may be used to provide information on default values to E2 Node.  The Policy Decision 35
indicates to the E2 Node, whether to accept or reject a RRM function, when the Policy conditions are met.  36
Examples include: 37
- Connected mode mobility policy, Handover Execution: Message Arrival breakpoint event trigger is defined to 38
initiate the Policy service. On the arrival of A3 Measurement Report, the Policy service kicks in. Policy service 39
installs a set of Policy Conditions like RSRP > ‘x’ db + Target Node Load < ‘x’ value + Number of successful 40
HO to target Node > ‘x’ value. When these Policy conditions are satisfied, then perform Policy Action -  41
“Execute HO” defined in the CONTROL service in Section 6.5. The Policy Action may be provided as a 42
standalone Policy Action ID “Execute HO” without any RAN parameters. As an alternative, Policy Action 43
“Execute HO” may be supplemented with default RAN parameters like Handover only QCI 5 and 9 bearers.  44
- Carrier Aggregation Policy, CA Release decision: A call process breakpoint event trigger is defined to initiate 45
the POLICY service. The call process breakpoint shall define conditions for Buffer occupancy. A call process 46

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.02
Copyright © 2022 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ
 18
breakpoint event shall be triggered when the Buffer Occupancy (BO) < ‘x’ KB. In this scenario, the event trigger 1
satisfies the Policy condition. Hence there is no need to define a Policy condition in the Policy service, When the 2
BO < ‘x’ KB kicks in, then Policy Action shall instruct E2 Node to “Release Scell” . 3
6.6.3 Policy Approach "Offset" 4
The "offset" Policy Approach is based on the design assumption that the Policy Action IE is used to carry one or more 5
RAN Parameters that are used to modify default E2 Node behaviour via the addition of an "offset" to be applied to 6
given target threshold or other parameter used in the target call process.   7
The applicable Policy Action is dependent upon a set of Policy Conditions and a given POLICY service may support 8
one or more Policy conditions and so provide a targeted Policy Action for a range of diffe rent specific cases, each 9
defined using a unique Policy condition where: 10
- Each Policy Condition is defined using a combination of RAN Parameters and conditional tests associated with 11
UE and Call process related information.  The first positive match in a list of Policy conditions is used to select 12
the corresponding Policy Action. 13
- Each Policy Action is defined using a list of RAN Parameters of data type INTEGER or REAL which may to 14
used directly for default values of type INTEGER or REAL (i.e. Default+Off set) and indirectly to for default 15
values of type ENUMERATED (i.e. select value in list that is Offset before or after default value).   16
Examples include: 17
- Connected mode mobility policy, Handover decision: A call process breakpoint event trigger is defined to 18
initiate the POLICY service from within the call process handling UE measurement reports related to handover 19
decisions for a specific target Slice and primary cell currently subject to Traffic Steering guidance.  The Policy 20
conditions list of RAN Parameters supports the definition of different A3 measurement threshold criteria offset 21
values to be applied to UEs with a specific combination of slice ID, active QoS bearers, velocity and throughput 22
and subject to overall E2 Node load and cell level load balancing requirements.  Handover is accepted if the 23
reported A3 measurement is greater than the default A3 measurement threshold+offset.  24
- Carrier Aggregation Policy, CA release decision: A call process breakpoint event trigger is defined to initiate the 25
POLICY service from within the call process related to Carrier Aggregation (CA) release decisions for a specific 26
target Slice currently subject to QoE guidance.  The Policy conditions list of RAN Parameters supports the 27
definition of different CA release threshold criteria offset values to be applied to UEs with a specific 28
combination of slice ID, active QoS bearers, velocity and throughput and subject to overall E2 Node load and 29
cell level load balancing requirements.  CA release is initiated if the UE thro ughput is less than the default UE 30
throughput threshold+offset. 31

- RIC CONTROL Service styles list along with the corresponding encoding type for each associated E2AP IE.  40

7.3.2 RIC Event trigger definition IE style 1: Message Event 9
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style is used to detect a specific Network Interface or RRC message event in E2 10
Node. The dection can be based on only for incoming or outgoing message. The E2 Node can also be configured to 11
detect multiple messages simultaneously and to trigger only when all the configured message events happen or for any 12
logical combination of message events.  13
Each message event configured can be further conditioned to be associated only for a certain UE or group of UEs as 14
indicated by the Associated UE Info IE if included, or only for some specific UE events defined in Section 8.1.5 as 15
indicated by the Associated UE Event IE if included. In case that the Global Associated UE Info IE is included, the 16
information is applied uniformly to all the message events configured and the IE shall override any Associated UE Info  17
IE included for some message events. 18
For each message event configured, Event Trigger Condition ID is assigned so that E2 Node can reply to Near -RT RIC 19
in the RIC INDICATION message to inform which event(s) are the cause for triggering. 20
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style uses RIC Event Trigger Definition IE Format 1 (9.2.1.1.1). 21

identifier and breakpoint identifier. The call process and breakpoint configured for event triggering can also be 24
conditioned to be associated with a certain E2 Node related information.  25

7.3.4 RIC Event trigger definition IE style 3: E2 Node Information Change 6
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style is used to detect E2 Node related information change from the subscribed E2 7
Node. The E2 Node can also be configured to detect multiple changes simultaneously and to trigger only when all the 8
configured changes happen or for any logical combination of the configured changes.  9
In this version of E2SM-RC specification, the following E2 Node related information changes are supported for eve nt 10
triggering.  11
E2 Node
Information
Change ID
E2 Node Information
Change Type
Description
1 Cell Configuration Change Triggered when any serving cell’s context information defined by
the Served Cell Information IE in TS 38.473 [19] clause 9.3.1.10
has changed.
2 Cell Neighbor Relation
Change
Triggered when any serving cell’s neighbor relation information
defined by Section 9.3.38 has changed.
3 Slice Configuration
Change
Triggered when slice configuration in any serving cell has changed.
Table 7.3.4-1: Event Trigger Definition Style 3 – Supported E2 Node information changes 12
Each E2 Node information change configured can also be conditioned to be associated with a specific cell or group of 13
cells for event triggering, as indicated by the Associated Cell Info IE if included.  14
For each information change configured for event triggering, Event Trigger Condition ID is also assigned so that E2 15
Node can reply to Near-RT RIC in the RIC INDICATION message to inform which event(s) are the cause for 16
triggering. 17
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style uses RIC Event Trigger Definition IE Format 3 (9.2.1.1.3). 18
7.3.5 RIC Event trigger definition IE style 4: UE Information Change 19
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style is used to detect UE Context related information change from the subscribed 20
E2 Node. The E2 Node can also be configured to detect multiple changes simultaneously and to trigger only when all 21
the configured changes happen or for any logical combination of the configured changes.  22
In this version of E2SM-RC specification, the supported UE Context information changes for event triggering are  23
- RRC state change 24
- UE identifier change (based on UE ID defined in Section 9.3.10)  25
- RLC/PDCP state variable or MAC state variable change (based on RAN Parameters defin ed in Sections 8.1.1.4 26
and 8.1.1.8) 27
For UE identifier change, the following cases are supported for event triggering.  28

7.3.6 RIC Event trigger definition IE style 5: On Demand 7
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style is used to be immediately triggered by E2 Node when a RIC subscription 8
having this event trigger is accepted. Once accepted, the E2 Node shall consider that this RIC subscription shall expire 9
automatically once all the requested actions for this RIC subscription are performed by the E2 Node.  10
The event can be further conditioned to be associated only for a certain UE or group of UEs as indicated by the 11
Associated UE Info IE if included, or for a specific cell or group of cells as indicated by the Associated Cell Info IE if 12
included. In this case, Near-RT RIC shall ensure that additional conditions imposed by the Associated UE Info IE or 13
Associated Cell Info IE does not prevent event triggering as soon as the RIC subscription is accepted by the E2 Node. 14
This RIC Event Trigger Definition IE style uses the RIC Event Trigger Definition IE Format 5 (9.2.1.1.5). 15

7.4 Supported RIC REPORT Services 17
7.4.1 REPORT Service style list 18
RIC Style Type Style Name Style Description
1 Message copy This style is used to report a copy of complete Network Interface or
RRC message.
2 Call Process Outcome This style is used to report the outcome of an ongoing call process.
3 E2 Node Information This style is used to report E2 Node information, Serving Cell
Configuration and Neighbour Relation related information.
4 UE Information This style is used to report the UE related information like PDCP,
RLC, MAC UE state variables and RRC UE State.
5 On Demand Report This style is used to report snapshot of UE related information and
Cell related information upon request from Near-RT RIC.

7.4.2 REPORT Service Style 1: Message Copy 20
7.4.2.1 REPORT Service Style description 21
This REPORT Service style provides the complete copy of a Network Interface or RRC message to be carried as a 22
transparent container in the RIC Indication Message IE. 23
This REPORT service style may also be used to report UE specific information associated with the Netw ork 24
Interface/RRC messages as provided in Section 8.2.1 RAN Parameters. Examples include reporting of UEID to Near -25
RT RIC when UE attaches to the E2 Node or when the UEID changes during Xn Handover, UE events like Secondary 26
Cell addition, Arrival of A3 Measurement Report (see Section 8.1.5 for the list of UE events).  27

7.4.6 REPORT Service Style 5: On Demand Report 18

received from Near-RT RIC:  21

- UE Context related information 24

information. The E2AP RIC Subscription Delete procedure or RIC Subscription Delete Required procedure [3] is not 26
required to delete this subscription. The reporting shall be per UE based or per cell based depending on the information 27
requested to be reported. 28

7.5.2 INSERT Service Style 1: Radio Bearer Control Request 11
7.5.2.1 INSERT Service Style description 12
This INSERT Service style provides a mechanism to initiate request to the RIC for controlling the functionalities of a 13
radio bearer related process pertaining to a UE using the RIC Indication Message IE and associated RIC Indication 14
Header IE. The E2 node sends a RIC Indication message to the near-RT RIC and the ongoing call process is suspended 15
at the E2 node until the E2 node hears back from the RIC. The optional RIC Call Process ID  IE is used by the E2 node 16
to match a RIC Control Request message to a RIC Indication message, following which the E2 node can resume the 17
suspended call processing for the UE.   18
Applications of this service include: 19
- Request for DRB QoS Modification, to tune DRB level QoS related parameters to meet the QoS optimization 20
targets. 21
- Request for QoS Flow (re)mapping, to adjust the mapping relationship between QoS flows and DRBs.  22
- Request for Logical channel (re)configuration 23

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.02
Copyright © 2022 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ
 27
- Request for Radio Bearer Admission Control, to configure DRB admission control such as reject or release may 1
be applied. 2
- Request for Split bearer and PDCP duplication control 3

7.5.2.2 INSERT Service RIC Action Definition IE contents 7
This INSERT Service style uses the RIC Action Definition IE Format 3 (9.2.1.2.3). This Insert style deals with the 8
supported Indication services, each service with a corresponding Indication ID listed in Section 7.5.2.1. The RAN 9
parameters, associated with each Insert RIC Indication service,  are included by the E2 node in the RIC Indication 10
message. Via the RIC Indication message, the E2 node seeks the near-RT RIC to accept or deny the request raised by 11
the E2 node and to accordingly set the values for the associated RAN parameters by the RIC via the control action in 12
the ensuing RIC Control Request message from the RIC. 13

request raised by the E2 node and accordingly set the values for the associated RAN parameters, via the control action 21

request raised by the E2 node and accordingly set the values for the associated RAN parameters, via the control action 4

7.5.5 INSERT Service Style 4: Radio Access Control Request 8
7.5.5.1 INSERT Service Style description 9
This INSERT Service style provides a mechanism to initiate request for controlling the radio access of the UE using the 10
RIC Indication Message IE and associated RIC Indication Header IE. The E2 node sends a RIC Indication message to 11
the near-RT RIC and the ongoing call process is suspended at the E2 node until the E2 node hears back from the RIC. 12
The optional RIC Call Process ID IE is used by the E2 node to match a RIC Control Request message to a RIC 13
Indication message, following which the E2 node can resume the suspended call processing for the UE . 14
Applications of this service include: 15
- Request for configuring RACH back-off 16
- Request for UE admission 17
- Request for RRC connection reject 18

7.5.9 INSERT Service Style 255: Multiple Actions Control Request 13
7.5.9.1 INSERT Service Style description 14
This INSERT Service style provides a mechanism  which contains multiple Insert Indication actions of the selected 15
fundamental level INSERT Service style(s), in order to initiate request to the Near-RT RIC for controlling multiple actions 16
of the supporting functionalities related to the corresponding fundamental level CONTROL Service style(s). If at least 17
one of the embedded Insert Indications is not admitted by E2 node, then the E2 node shall declare the INSERT Action as 18
failed. 19
7.5.9.2 INSERT Service RIC Action Definition IE contents 20
This INSERT Service style uses the RIC Action Definition IE Format 4 (9.2.1.2.4).  21
For each Insert Indication action, the corresponding Insert Indication ID IE and the associated RAN parameters follow 22
the definitions of the selected fundamental level INSERT Service style indicated by the Requested Insert Style IE. 23
7.5.9.3 INSERT Service RIC Indication Header IE contents 24
This INSERT Service style uses RIC Indication Header IE Format 3 (9.2.1.3.3).  25
The RIC Indication Header IE may contain the UE ID IE, to indicate to the Near-RT RIC that this INSERT indication 26
is only for that specific UE. 27
7.5.9.4 INSERT Service RIC Indication Message IE contents 28
This INSERT Service style uses RIC Indication Message IE Format 6 (9.2.1.4.6).  29
For each Insert Indication action, the corresponding Insert Indication ID IE and the associated RAN parameters follow 30
the definitions of the selected fundamental level INSERT Service style indicated by the Indicated Insert Style IE. 31

This INSERT Service style uses RIC Call Process ID IE Format 1 (9.2.1.5.1). 33

7.6 Supported RIC CONTROL Services 1
7.6.1 CONTROL Service Style Types 2
RIC Style Type Style Name Style Description
1 Radio Bearer control Used to modify the configuration the Radio Bearer Control (RBC)
related parameters and/or behaviours at the E2 Node for a
specific UE
Belongs to Fundamental level CONTROL Services.
2 Radio resource allocation
control
Used to modify the configuration the Radio Resource Allocation
control related parameters and/or behaviours at the E2 Node for a
specific E2 Node, cell, slice, UE and/or QoS
Belongs to Fundamental level CONTROL Services.
3 Connected mode mobility
control
Used to initiate a connected mode mobility procedure (Handover
or Conditional Handover), optionally with Dual Active Protocol
Stack (DAPS), for a specific UE towards either a target cell (for
HO) or a list of candidate cells (for CHO)
Belongs to Fundamental level CONTROL Services.
4 Radio access control Used to modify Radio access related functions used to control UE
access to cells
Belongs to Fundamental level CONTROL Services.
5 Dual connectivity (DC) control Used to initiate Dual connectivity (DC) mechanisms
Belongs to Fundamental level CONTROL Services.
6 Carrier Aggregation (CA)
control
Used to initiate Carrier Aggregation (CA) mechanisms
Belongs to Fundamental level CONTROL Services.
7 Idle mode mobility control Used to modify Idle mode mobility related functions used to control
UE reselection of cells
Belongs to Fundamental level CONTROL Services.
8 UE information and
assignment
Used for Explicit UE list assignment, UE information report
generation and to complete UE identification.  These services are
used to support other RIC services.
Belongs to Fundamental level CONTROL Services.
9 Measurement Reporting
Configuration control
Used to control the measurement report configuration
255 Multiple Actions Control Used for multiple actions of the selected fundamental level
CONTROL Service style(s).
Belongs to lntegrated level CONTROL Services.
 3
Each of the Control Service styles 1-9 listed above points to adopt the following common features: 4
- Control Action ID: The index ID for the individual control action under a given Control Service style.  5
- Control Action Name: Indicates the functionality of the E2 node which is controlled by Near -RT RIC 6
- Control Action Description: Describes the control action and functionality of the receiving E2 Node.  7
- Associated RAN parameters: Identifies the RAN parameters to be controlled by Near -RT RIC pertaining to the 8
given control action. 9
The Control Service style 255 supports multiple parallel actions configured per RIC Control Request message by 10
reusing the control actions and the associated RAN parameters defined in the selected fundamental level Control 11
Service style(s). 12
 13
The details of the individual Control Service styles are provided in subsequent sections. 14

7.6.2.2 CONTROL Service RIC Control Header IE contents 11
This CONTROL Service RIC Control Header IE has the UE ID IE, the Control Service Style ID, the Control Action 12
ID IE and the RIC Control Decision IE that indicates whether the RIC accepts or rejects the INDICATION request from 13
the previous incoming INSERT indication, if any (with matching RAN Call Process ID IE), from the E2 node.  14
This CONTROL style uses RIC Control Header IE Format 1 (9.2.1.6.1). 15
7.6.2.3 CONTROL Service RIC Control Message IE contents 16
This CONTROL Service RIC Control Message IE contains the sequence of RAN parameters, associated with a given 17
Control Action within this Control Service style, controlled by the near-RT RIC along with the values for these 18
parameters, as set by the RIC. 19
This CONTROL style uses RIC Control Message IE Format 1 (9.2.1.7.1). 20
 21
If there is a previous INSERT Indication Request to the RIC, then the corresponding Control Action ID used by the RIC 22
for the ensuing CONTROL Request message is the one that matches the Insert Indication ID, among the ones provided 23
in the table shown in Section 7.6.2.1.  It is to be noted that the control action “Radio admission control” (corresponding 24
to control action ID 4) is used only as a response to an incoming INSERT indic ation with the corresponding service 25
style and indication request ID and cannot be used asynchronously without a previous INSERT indication. 26

processing upon receiving the message.   8

7.6.10 CONTROL Service Style 255: Multiple Actions Control 7
7.6.10.1 CONTROL Service Style description 8
This CONTROL Service style provides a mechanism to initiate multiple control actions of the selected fundamental 9
level CONTROL Service style(s) that should be processed in an integrated manner by the E2 Node, i.e. the RIC Control 10
procedure is considered failed if at least one of the indicated control actions is unsuccessfully executed, and RIC 11
CONTROL FAILURE message shall be sent containing the RIC Control Outcome for failed Control Action. 12
7.6.10.2 CONTROL Service RIC Control Header IE contents 13
This CONTROL style uses RIC Control Header IE Format 2 (9.2.1.6.2). 14
The RIC Indication Header IE may contain the UE ID IE to indicate to the E2 Node that this control request is only for 15
that specific UE. The RIC Control Decision IE may also be included to indicate to the E2 Node whether the Near -RT 16
RIC accepts or rejects the INDICATION request from the previous incoming INSERT indication,  if any (with matching 17
RAN Call Process ID IE), from the E2 node.  18
7.6.10.3 CONTROL Service RIC Control Message IE contents 19
This CONTROL style uses RIC Control Message IE Format 2 (9.2.1.7.2).  20
The RAN control actions and the corresponding RAN parameters under a fundamental level Control Service style 21
contained in the RIC Control Message IE follows the definitions of the indicated Control Service style.  22
If this control request is sent as a response to a previous INSERT indication from the E2 node, then the Control Action 23
ID IE in the RIC Control Message IE is set in accordance with the triggered Insert Indication ID. 24
7.6.10.4 CONTROL Service RIC Call Process ID IE contents 25
This CONTROL Service style uses RIC Call Process ID IE Format 1 (9.2.1.5.1). 26
The optional RIC Call Process ID IE is used when resuming a call process following a previous INSERT indication 27
from the E2 Node. 28
7.6.10.5 CONTROL Service RIC Control Outcome IE contents 29
This CONTROL style uses RIC Control Outcome IE Format 2 (9.2.1.8.2). 30

7.7 Supported RIC POLICY Services 7
7.7.1 POLICY Service style list 8
RIC Style Type Style Name Style Description
1 Policy for Radio Bearer
control
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of Radio
Bearer Control (RBC) of call processes for a specific RAN UE
Group based on cell, slice, UE list and/or QoS
2 Policy for Radio resource
allocation control
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of Radio
Resource Allocation control of call processes for a specific RAN
UE Group based on cell, slice, UE list and/or QoS
3 Policy for Connected mode
mobility control
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of connected
mode mobility procedure (Handover or Conditional Handover),
optionally with Dual Active Protocol Stack (DAPS), call processes
for a specific RAN UE Group based on cell, slice, UE list and/or
QoS
4 Policy for Radio access
control
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of radio access
control processes
5 Policy for Dual connectivity
(DC) control
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of dual
connectivity (DC) call processes for a specific RAN UE Group
based on cell, slice, UE list and/or QoS
6 Policy for Carrier Aggregation
(CA) control
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of carrier
aggregation (CA) call processes for a specific RAN UE Group
based on cell, slice, UE list and/or QoS
7 Policy for Idle mode mobility
control
Used to define a policy for modifying the behaviour of idle mode
configuration call processes for a specific RAN UE Group based
on cell, slice and/or UE list.
8 Policy for Measurement
Reporting Configuration
Control
Used to define a policy for configuration of measurement objects
and reporting objects
 9
Each of the POLICY Service Styles 1-8 listed above are supported using the following common features: 10
• Event Trigger: POLICY service is initiated by either Event Trigger style 1: Message Event or Event Trigger 11
style 2: Call process breakpoint. 12
• A ction ID : The index ID for the individual action under a given POLICY Service style. 13
• A ction Name : Indicates the functionality of the E2 node which is controlled by Near-RT RIC 14
• A ction Description : Describes the action and functionality of the receiving E2 Node. 15
• A ssociated RAN parameters: Identifies the RAN parameters to be controlled by Near -RT RIC pertaining to the 16
given Policy action, used to define Policy Condition and RAN Imperative Policy. 17
All POLICY Service styles use RIC Action Definition IE Format 2 (9.2.1.2.2) which provides the policy conditions and 18
corresponding Policy Action. All of these factors are defined as a sequence of RAN Parameters assigned according to a 19
given Policy Style and Policy Action where: 20
- Policy Action ID is a Policy specific identifier of a specific Action for a specific Policy style. 21
- Policy Condition is a Policy specific condition to select a specific Policy Action. Policy Condition is described in 22
terms of a list of test conditions concerning UE and E2 Node information selection criteria using RAN 23

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.02
Copyright © 2022 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ
 50
Parameters defined with a Conditional Criteria Definition. Default RAN behaviour is to be applied to any UE 1
when none of the Policy conditions are met. 2
- Policy Action is encoded in terms of a list of specific RAN Parameters and shall be applied to any UE that meets 3
a specific Policy Condition. Policy Action may contain optional Policy Decision to indicate acceptance or 4
rejection of a RRM function when the Policy Conditions are met. 5
The details of the individual POLICY Service Styles and specific Policy Actions are provided in subsequent sections.  6
7.7.2 POLICY Service Style 1: Radio Bearer Control 7
7.7.2.1 POLICY Service Style description 8
This POLICY Service style provides an Imperative Policy to control execution of a radio bearer control related 9
process.   10
Applications of this service include: 11
- DRB QoS Modification, to tune DRB level QoS related parameters to meet the QoS optimization  targets. 12
- QoS Flow mapping, to adjust the mapping relationship between QoS flows and DRBs.  13
- Logical channel configuration 14
- Radio Bearer Admission, to guide DRB admission control algorithms for admission and/or rejection of DRB 15
requests 16
- DRB termination 17
- DRB Split bearer 18
- PDCP duplication control 19

 58
8 RAN Parameter assignments 1
8.0 Approach 2
The RAN parameters associated with each RIC service  described in Section 7 are listed  here in Section 8 .  Each RAN 3
parameter belongs to one of the following value types: 4
• ELEMENT: a singleton variable, which does not have any other associated RAN parameters. 5
• STRUCTURE: a sequence of RAN parameters, each of which can be either an ELEMENT or a STRUCTURE 6
or a LIST 7
• LIST: a list of STRUCTURES, where each STRUCTURE is as defined above. The sequence of RAN parameters 8
is the same across all the STRUCTURES within the list. 9
The corresponding 3GPP standard definitions of these RAN parameters (if available) are referenced in the tables below 10
under the “RAN Parameter Definition” column. These RAN parameters having 3GPP standard definitions are not freshly 11
defined or redefined here.  12
Note that only those RAN parameters identified as ELEMENT are subject to test conditions by the RIC in the “Event 13
Trigger Definition”.  14
Any RAN parameter within a STRUCTURE or LIST shall not be referenced individually. Hierarchy of a LIST or a 15
STRUCTURE shall be traversed to access any RAN parameter within the LIST or STRUCTURE  16
Note that a RAN parameter may be associated with as a key where its corresponding Key Flag  is set to “TRUE”. These 17
RAN parameters serve as a reference to other RAN parameters within a structure that may be a part of LIST to enable 18
the E2 Node interpret the scope of RAN parameters that are controlled by Near -RT RIC. 19
If the “key flag” is specified in the RIC Event Trigger Definition, then the RAN parameters corresponding to “that specific 20
itemized structure” in the list indexed by the “key flag” are subject to test condition, but if the “key flag” is not mentioned 21
in the RIC Event Trigger Definition, then the RAN parameters corresponding to “any itemized structure” within the list 22
are subject to test condition.  23
For e.g., The ‘QFI’ can be considered a ‘key parameter’ to identify a QoS flow among the list of flows in a UE -specific 24
PDU session. If the QFI parameter is NOT mentioned and the RIC subscribes to an event pertaining to 5QI 8, then “any 25
QoS flow” in the list of flows of a PDU session for the UE that matches the condition of 5QI being equal to 8 would be 26
covered by this event trigger definition. On the other hand, if the QFI parameter is mentioned in the event trigger 27
definition, then only that specific QoS flow pertaining to the indicated QFI within the list is covered  28
8.1 RAN parameters for Event Trigger 29
The RAN Parameters pertaining to “Event Trigger” that are used across multiple service styles are listed here. All RAN 30
Parameters defined in section 8.1 may also be used to define Policy Condition, see also section 8.5.  31

8.3.9.2 E2 Node Context Information 1
The associated RAN parameters are given in Section 8.1.1.11. 2
8.3.10 Indication Semantics Description for interpretation by the RIC 3
The E2 node requests the near-RT RIC for the following services as far as the radio bearer Control request is concerned.  4
(a) In the RIC Indication Header IE, the E2 node indicates the Insert Indication ID, that is associated with the Insert 5
Service Style ID for the radio bearer control request, along with the UE ID, so as to enable the RIC to interpret 6
which Insert Indication service pertaining to which UE is being requested by the E2 node.  7
(b) In the RIC Indication Message IE, the E2 node indicates the list of the RAN parameters in the Indication 8
message that it wants to be controlled by the near-RT RIC. If the E2 node does not provide values for these 9
parameters in the RIC Indication message IE, then the RIC would set the values for these parameters in the 10
control action sent via the RIC Control Request message, along with its decision to accept/deny the request 11
raised by the E2 node (indicated in the RIC Indication Header IE). If the RAN parameter indicated by the E2 12
node is an ELEMENT, the RIC would set the value for the parameter in its RIC Control Request message. If the 13
indicated RAN parameter is a STRUCTURE but if the E2 node does not list any constitutent RAN parameter of 14
the STRUCTURE, then the RIC would set the values for all the constitutent RAN parameters of the 15
STRUCTURE. If the parameter is a LIST, then: 16
a. If the E2 node also indicates the Key RAN parameter pertaining to the itemized STRUCTURE in the 17
LIST, then the RIC would set the values for all constituent RAN parameters within the structure, pointed 18
by the key. 19
b. If the E2 node does not indicate the Key RAN parameter pertaining to the itemized STRUCTURE in the 20
LIST, then the RIC would set the values for all constituent RAN parameters within eac h itemized 21
STRUCTURE, whose key RAN parameter is identified by the RIC. 22
(c) If the E2 node provides values for these parameters in the RIC Indication message IE, then the RIC would set the 23
values only for those indicated parameters for which it would choos e to replace the values already set by the E2 24
node. It also communicates its decision to accept/deny the request raised by the E2 node for the DRB.  25
(d) Any RAN parameter identified as a key shall always carry a value set by the E2 node, if the E2 node expects the 26
RIC to control the parameters pertaining to the STRUCTURE pointed by the E2 node. The value of this key 27
RAN parameter is an index that points to the entire STRUCTURE, and hence the value of the key RAN 28
parameter cannot be modified by the near-RT RIC. Without indicating the value for the key RAN parameter, the 29
RIC would not control the parameters associated with the structure indexed by the key . 30
Note that the RIC can only set the values for those RAN parameters identified as ELEMENT when they are in dicated 31
by the E2 node; however, these RAN parameters can be contained with a STRUCTURE or within an itemized 32
STRUCTURE in a LIST. Also, if the DRB ID key parameter is not present for any DRB in the RIC Indication Message 33
IE, then the RIC would discard the RIC Indication message. And the E2 node would have to set values based on its 34
default radio resource management policies upon time out, and continue with the ongoing call processing. Hence, 35
indicating the DRB ID IE for the DRB(s) is a pre-requisite for the RIC to act on the Insert indication via its RIC Control 36
Request message. 37

8.4.2.6 DRB Split Ratio Control 1
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message, in the presence of Downlink PDCP Data Split IE, the E2 node shall 2
split the downlink PDCP traffic between the Master Node and Secondary Node over the X2/Xn interface based on the 3
recommended ratio. In the presence of Uplink PDCP Data Split Threshold IE, the E2 node shall invoke procedures 4
related to DRB Split Ratio Control, such as Bearer Context Management, UE Context Management, RRC Message 5
Transfer, etc. and include the IEs corresponding to one or more of parameters described below in the related interface 6
messages. If the DRB ID is missing in the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node will send a RIC Control Failure .  7
RAN

8.4.2.7 PDCP Duplication Control 9
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node shall invoke procedures related to PDCP Duplication 10
Control, such as Bearer Context Management, UE Context Management, RRC Message Transfer, etc. and include the 11
IEs corresponding to one or more of parameters described below in the rel ated interface messages. If the DRB ID is 12
missing in the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node will send a RIC Control Failure . 13

8.4.3.6 Slice-level PRB quota 2
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node allocates slice-specific PRB quota for the indicated S-3
NSSAI in terms of the maximum PRB allocation ratio, minimum PRB allocation ratio and dedicated PRB allocation 4
ratio for the given slice among the available set of PRBs. If the S-NSSAI is missing in the RIC Control Request message, 5
the E2 node will send a RIC Control Failure. 6

8.4.4 Connected Mode Mobility Control 3
8.4.4.1 Handover Control 4
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message, in the case of Xn/X2 or NG or inter-RAT handovers, the E2 node 5
shall invoke procedures, such as Handover Preparation related to UE Mobility Management, Bearer Context 6
Modification, UE Context Modification, RRC Message Transfer, etc. In the case of intra-gNB or F1 handover, the E2 7
node shall invoke procedures, such as UE Context Modification, RRC Message Transfer, etc. The E2 node includes the 8
IEs corresponding to one or more of parameters described below in the related interface messages. If the Target 9
Primary Cell ID IE is missing in the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node will send a RIC Control Failure 10
message. 11

8.4.4.2 Conditional Handover Control 2
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message, in the case of Xn/X2 or NG or inter-RAT conditional handovers, the 3
E2 node shall invoke procedures, such as Handover Preparation related to UE Mobility Management, Bearer Context 4
Modification, UE Context Modification, RRC Message Transfer, etc. involving the candidate target cells (note that there 5
is only one Handover Preparation in the case of NG or inter-RAT handovers). In the case of intra-gNB or F1 6
conditional handover, the E2 node shall invoke procedures, such as UE Context Modification , RRC Message Transfer, 7
etc. The E2 node includes the IEs corresponding to one or more of parameters described below in the related interface 8
messages. If the Target Cell IE is missing in the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node will send a RIC Control 9
Failure message. 10

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.02

procedures, such as Handover Preparation related to UE Mobility Management, Bearer Context Modification, UE 4
Context Modification, RRC Message Transfer, etc. In the case of intra-gNB or F1 DAPS handover, the E2 node shall 5
invoke procedures, such as UE Context Modification, RRC Message Transfer, etc. The E2 node includes the IEs 6
corresponding to one or more of parameters described below in the related interface messages. If the Target Primary 7
Cell ID IE is missing in the RIC Control Request message, the E2 node will send a RIC Control Failure messag e. 8

8.4.6.3 PSCell Change control for Secondary Cell Group 2
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message, in the case of intra-SN PSCell change, the E2 node shall invoke 3
procedures related to PSCell Change Control, such as Dual Connectivity Secondary Node Modification, UE Context 4
Modification, RRC Message Transfer, etc. In the case of inter-SN PSCell change, the E2 node shall invoke procedures 5
such as Dual Connectivity Secondary Node Release (MN/SN-initiated) or SN Change (only SN-initiated), Bearer 6
Context Modification, UE Context Modification, RRC Message Transfer, etc. The E2 node then includes the IEs 7
corresponding to one or more of parameters described below in the related interface messages.  8

8.4.10  Measurement Reporting Configuration Control 6
8.4.10.1  Add MR Configuration 7
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message with the Measurement Report Configuration Control Service Style and 8
the Add MR Configuration control action, the E2 node shall invoke relevant RRC procedures to configure Measurement 9
Report to the UE.  E2 Node shall include the IEs corresponding to one or more of RAN parameters described below  in 10
the related RRC or NI interface messages.  11

8.4.10.2  Modify MR Configuration 2
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message with the Measurement Report Configuration Control Service Style and 3
the Modify MR Configuration control action, the E2 node shall invoke RRC procedures related to MR Configuration, 4
include the IEs corresponding to one or more of parameters described below in the related NI interface messages or RRC 5
message. 6

8.4.10.3  Delete MR Configuration 2
Upon receiving the RIC Control Request message with the Measurement Report Configuration Control Service Style and 3
the Modify MR Configuration control action , the E2 node shall invoke RRC procedures related to  deletion of  MR 4
Configuration and include the IEs corresponding to one or more of parameters described below in the related interface or 5
RRC  messages.  6

8.5 RAN parameters for POLICY services 4
8.5.1 Approach 5
The RAN parameters associated with each policy action being controlled by Near -RT RIC described in Section 7.7 are 6
listed.   7
There are two types of E2 policies: 8
i) Control action policy: In this type, the near-RT RIC tells the E2 node on the specific per-UE control action that 9
needs to be performed, upon meeting a given policy condition for a given UE or a group of UEs, for a given cell 10
and/or for a given E2 node. This policy type is descriptive in nature. The control action is defined with respect to 11
individual UEs and UE-specific bearers, flows, PDU sessions, etc.  12
ii) Offset based policy: In this type, the near-RT RIC offers a generic prescriptive guidance to the E2 node on how 13
it shall deviate from default behaviour via the application of offset parameters provided in the POLICY Action 14
IE. Different POLICY Action IEs are associated with different POLICY conditions described in terms of UE and 15
E2 Node characteristics. As defined in section 6.6.3, offset parameters are to be applied to default parameters 16
according to the following rules: 17
- INTEGER and REAL default parameters: Offset parameter have the same data type as default parameter and 18
is added to default parameter with positive offset parameter values increasing default value and negative 19
offset parameter values decreasing default value.  That is, policy modifies the target call process such that:  20
Value to be applied = (Default Parameter) + (Offset Parameter)- ENUMERATED parameters: Offset 21
parameter are of data type INTEGER and are used to select a different item in the ENUMERATED list, 22
positive offset parameter values used to select items that are further on in the list, zero offset parameter 23
values used to select the default value, negative offset parameter values used to select items that are earlier on 24
in the list.  When and if the offset parameter value results in the selection of an item in the ENUMERATED 25
list that exceeds the ENUMERATED list length then the last item in the list is selected.  When and if the 26
offset parameter value results in the selection of an item in the ENUMERATED list that prior to the first item 27
in the ENUMERATED list then the first item in the list is selected.  That is, policy modifies the target call 28
process such that: 29
ENUMERATED List index = MIN [List length-1, MAX [0, (Default Parameter) + (Offset Parameter)] ] 30

9.3 Information Element definitions 2
9.3.1 General 3
When specifying information elements which are to be represented by bit strings, if not otherwise specifically stated in 4
the semantics description of the concerned IE or elsewhere, the following principle applies with regards to the ordering 5
of bits: 6
- The first bit (leftmost bit) contains the most significant bit (MSB); 7
- The last bit (rightmost bit) contains the least significant bit (LSB); 8
- When importing bit strings from other specifications, the first bit of the bit string contains the first bit of the 9
concerned information. 10
9.3.2 RAN Function Name 11
This IE is defined in [4] clause 6.2.2.1. 12
9.3.3 RIC Style Type 13
This IE is defined in [4] clause 6.2.2.2. 14
9.3.4 RIC Style Name 15
This IE is defined in [4] clause 6.2.2.3. 16
9.3.5 RIC Format Type 17
This IE is defined in [4] clause 6.2.2.4. 18

reference

>ELEMENT with Key Flag
TRUE
   If the RAN parameter is singular variable
and if it is a key parameter with key flag
set to TRUE as in Section 8.
>>RAN Parameter Value M  9.3.14 This IE must be filled for both INSERT
and CONTROL if the key flag is TRUE
so as to reference the proper structure
within the list.
>ELEMENT with Key Flag
FALSE
   If the RAN parameter is singular variable
and if it is NOT a key parameter (key flag
set to FALSE). as in Section 8.
>>RAN Parameter Value C-ifControl  9.3.14 This IE must be filled if this structure is
part of a RIC Control Request message;
else, if it is part of a RIC Indication
message, this IE is optional.
>STRUCTURE    If the RAN parameter is a structure, in
turn containing a set of RAN parameters.
>>RAN Parameter Structure M  9.3.12

individual items, each of which has an
index.

9.4 Information Element Abstract Syntax (with ASN.1) 1
9.4.1 General 2
E2SM-RC ASN.1 definition conforms to ITU-T Rec. X.680 [5] and ITU-T Rec. X.681 [6]. 3
Sub clause 9.4.2 presents the Abstract Syntax of the E2SM information elements to be carried  within the E2AP [3] 4
protocol messages with ASN.1. In case there is contradiction between the ASN.1 definition in this sub clause and the 5
tabular format in sub clause 9.2 and 9.3, the ASN.1 shall take precedence, except for the definition of conditions for the 6
presence of conditional elements, in which the tabular format shall take precedence. 7
If an E2SM information element carried as an OCTET STRING in an E2AP [3] mes sage that is not constructed as 8
defined above is received, this shall be considered as Abstract Syntax Error, and the message shall be handled as 9
defined for Abstract Syntax Error in clause 9. 10
9.4.2 Information Element Definitions 11

Annex A: Examples on IE Contents 1
A.1 Introduction 2
This annex presents example applications of selected use cases showing alternative solutions using different 3
combinations of RIC Services Report, Insert, Control and/or Policy. 4
A.2 Connected mode mobility based on UE measurement report 5
A.2.1 Assumptions 6
This example is based on the following assumptions: 7
1 O- CU-CP, or gNB for aggregated deployments, has E2 interface to Near -RT RIC and supports one or more RIC 8
services using E2SM-RC. 9
2 UE is in RRC CONNECTED state using NR access and has successfully attached to a 5G Core Network (5GC)  10
3 UE has been previously configured to send RRC Measurement Reports. 11
4 UE sends a RRC Measurement Report containing one or more neighbour cell measurements applicable for an 12
inter-cell connected mode mobility event (i.e. a Handover) 13
5 O- CU-CP, or gNB for aggregated deployments, uses one or more RIC Services to complete the handover 14
decision and either execute handover (i.e. using procedure described in 3GPP 38.300 section 9.2.3) or ignores 15
measurement report. 16
Step 5 may be realized using one or more of the following solutions: 17
i) According to a previously established RIC Subscription procedure, the arrival of the RRC Measurement Report 18
triggers an Event Trigger which results in the E2 Node suspending the ongoing call process and sending a RIC 19
Service INSERT message to the Near-RT RIC.  The Near-RT RIC takes the Handover Decision and sends a RIC 20
Service CONTROL message carrying the response which is used by the E2 node to resume the call process.   21
ii) According to a previously established RIC Subscription procedure the arrival of the RRC Measurement Report 22
triggers an Event Trigger which results in the E2 Node executing a RIC Service POLICY which is used to 23
modify the default Handover Decision and so modifies the remaining steps in the ongoing call proc ess.  24
 25
A.2.2 Solution using RIC Services Insert and Control  26
Editor’s Note: FFS 27
A.2.3 Solution using RIC Service Policy ("Offset" based approach) 28
This section provides a solution for the Connected Mode Mobility event call flow using the RIC Service Policy using 29
the “Offset” approach.  Corresponding example message content are provided for the RIC Event Trigger Definition  IE 30
and RIC Action Definition IE contents for the Connected Mode Mobility service (Policy Style 3) sent from the RIC to 31
the E2 node to establish a policy used to provide guidance for the handling of incoming RRC Measurement reports from 32
a UE connected to a 5GC network using Standalone (SA) access. 33
A2.3.1 Assumptions 34
This example is based on the following design assumptions: 35
1 Event trigger defined using Style 2 (Call Process Breakpoint), Type 3 (Mobility Management) and Id 1 36
(handover Preparation) with the assumption that this breakpoint corresponds to the point of the UE call process 37
code in a gNB where a handover decision is to be taken based on a received RRC Measurement report. 38

ORAN.WG3.E2SM-RC-v01.02
Copyright © 2022 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ
 333
a. Event Trigger Definition IE RAN parameters for Associated E2 Node Info IE are not used 1
b. Event Trigger Definition IE RAN parameters for Associated UE Info IE are used to offer filtering of UE 2
between those subject to Policy handling and those to be handled using default parameters.  In this example 3
RAN parameters for discrimination based on Slice and Group (aka SPID) are described.  4
2 Policy defined using Style 3 (Connected Mobile Mobility), Policy Action ID 1 (Policy for Handover control)  5
a. Policy Condition Definition IE RAN parameters used to map UE to an appropriate Policy Action.  In this 6
example RAN parameters based on Serving Cell and Explicit UE List membership are described.   7
b. Policy Action Definition IE parameters used to define a set of offsets (+positive, zero or -negative values) to 8
be applied to default measurement thresholds to calculate policy modified threshold used during Handover 9
decision prior to Handover execution. 10
3 Depending upon the outcome of the decision the gNB either: 11
a. Proceeds with handover execution using information obtained from the measurement report, stored UE 12
context information and result of subsequent network transactions 13
b. Ignores measurement report and continues any other required call processing  14

A.2.3.2 RIC Event Trigger Definition IE contents 1
RIC Event Trigger Definition IE contains RAN Parameter lists for Associated E2 Node Info IE and Associated UE info 2
IE.  In this example, only the Associated UE info IE is used where the set of target UEs for the event is defined by a 3
given slice (SST=sst1, SD=sd1) and group (IRFSP=irfsp1) 4
Additional sets of target UEs may be supported using the same RAN Parameter list with different target values for SST, 5
SD and IRFSP.  These would be combined within the Associated E2 Node Info IE using the optional "Logical OR" flag 6
(see section 9.3.26). 7
The contents of the RAN Parameter Testing for UE Group IE (defined in 8.1.3) for the above scenario are as follows: 8
RAN Parameter
ID
Value type Key flag Value Test condition Semantics Description
10 STRUCTURE    S-NSSAI
11 ELEMENT FALSE sst1 equal >SST
12 ELEMENT FALSE sd1 equal >SD
20 STRUCTURE    Group ID
21 ELEMENT FALSE Irfsp1 equal >IRFSP
 9
A.2.3.3 RIC Action Definition IE contents 10
RIC Action Definition IE contains RAN Parameter lists for Policy Condition Definition IE and Policy Action Definition 11
IE.   12
In this example the Policy Condition Definition IE is used to define the set of target UEs that are to be assigned a given 13
Policy Action Definition IE based on a given Serving Cell (nr-cgi1) and membership of a given Explicit UE List 14
(HOList1).  The corresponding Policy Action Definition IE is used to set the measurement threshold offset for A3 RSRP 15
measurement threshold (A3-rsrp-off1) 16
Different values of NR-CGI and/or Explicit UE List ID may be used in each Policy condition in the Action Definition  17
IE, each with a corresponding different Policy Action definition. 18
The contents of the Policy Condition Definition IE (defined using RAN parameters in sections 8.5.4 and 8.1.3) for the 19
above scenario are as follows: 20
RAN Parameter
ID
Value type Key flag Value Test condition Semantics Description

502 STRUCTURE    >Serving cell item
503 STRUCTURE    >>CHOICE Serving Cell

505 ELEMENT FALSE nr-cgi1 equal >>>>Serving NR CGI
30 ELEMENT FALSE HOList1 Equal Explicit UE List ID
